[TD 264]

ORAN DO REISIMEID EARRA-GHAIDHEAL

A rìgh, gur mi tha aighearach
Mu ’n naidheachd seo tha ùr ann;
Tha m’ inntinn air a h-àrdachadh				3870
On thàinig fir mo dhùthcha.
Guidheam-sa buaidh-làrach leibh
’S gach àit an loisg sibh fùdar,
Toil-inntinn aig ’ur càirdean
’S ’ur nàimhdean a bhith tùirseach.				3875

’N uair thàinig Mormhair Fréderic
Thug Dùn Eideann cliù dha;
Gur cònspull air cheann sluaigh e
’N uair ghluaiseas iad r’ a chùlaibh:
Sàr cheann-feadhna treubhach				3880
’S e léirsinneach ’gan stiùradh,
Ag imeachd leis an réisimeid,
’S e féin a’ dèanamh iùil daibh.

Tha oifhichearan gasda
Cho math ’s a tha fo ’n chrùn ann;				3885
’S math a thig an airm-ghaisge dhaibh,
’S iad fasanda ’gan giùlan;
’S toil-inntinne r’ am faicinn
Na lasgairean glan’ ùra,
’N uair thog iad pìob is brataichean				3890
Air machraichean nan Dùbhghall.

Is ìnnsidh mi le barantas,
On a b’ aithne dhomh o thùs sibh,
Air chruas an àit an tachair sibh,
Cha cheum air ais ’ur dùthchas:				3895
Sliochd nan curaidh calma
Bh’ anns na h-armailtean bha cliùiteach,
Ri ’n goireadh càch na h-Earra-Ghaidh’laich,
’S am fearg cha bu chùis shùgraidh.

[TD 265]

[Beurla]

[TD 266]

Tha buaidh air feachd Earra-Ghàidheal,			3900
Cha ghabh iad sgàth no cùram:
’S iad neartmhor beachdail àrdanach,
Gu reachdmhor làidir lùthmhor;
’S daoin’-uaisle ceart tha fàs ann,
Nach ’eil fàilinneach no lùbach;				3905
’S neo-sheachantach na h-àrmainn sin,
Ag iomain chàich gu ’n dùbhlan.

’S math thig dol ’nan éideadh dhaibh,
’S tha reusan air a’ chùis ud:
Tha gunnachan deagh-ghleusd’ aca,				3910
’S chan ’eil té dhiubh dhiùltas;
An crios-gualainn féin orra,
’S an claidheamh glé-gheur cùil ann;
Bu mhath an am an fheuma iad
’N uair a leumadh sibh g’ an rùsgadh.			3915

Tha iad leathan mu na broillichean,
Fir chothromach ’s iad dùmhail,
Le ’n calpanna deas dìreach,
’S iad lìontach fo na glùinean;
Osain ghoirid bhreaca						3920
Le dreach air an cur ùmpa,
’S math thig gartain chàrnaid daibh,
As fheàrr a th’ anns na bùithean.

Is lìonmhor baintighearn’ innealta
Nach sireadh i le dùrachd					3925
Ach cead bhith anns na bileidean
’S na gillean seo bhith dlùth dhaibh,
A bheireadh pòg le sireadh dhaibh
Cho milis ris an t-siùcar,
’S a bheireadh mìltean dolar dhaibh,				3930
’S na sporanan g’ an giùlan.

Tha suaicheantas na h-Alb’ agaibh,
Is dh’ fhalbh sibh leis gu sùnndach,
Am fothannan cruaidh calgarra,
’S neo-chearbach cur a’ chrùin air:				3935

[TD 267]

[Beurla]

[TD 268]

An luibh as gairge riasgaiche
A bha riamh a measg nam flùran;
Is ceann na muice fiadhaiche
A leag Diarmaid ’sa’ choill ùdlaidh.

’S e thubhairt na bha ’g amharc oirbh				3940
An latha bha ’n rebhiù ann,
Gum bu fhreagarrach ’ur làmhach
’N uair a thàirngeadh sibh na rùdain;
B’ fharamach ’ur gluasad
A’ tarraing suas gu siùbhlach;					3945
’S am breacan cruinn an fhéile
Air sléisdean geal nam fiùran.

Is flathail na daoin’ uaisl’ a th’ ann,
’S neul cruadail air gach aoinfhear;
Na saighdearan deas cumachdail,				3950
’S gach duine dhiubh cho ionnsaicht’:
Nam bitheadh càs no cunnart ann,
Có b’ urrainn g’ a thoirt dhiùbh-san?
’S i ’n réisimeid as urramaich’
A chunnaic mi le m’ shùilean.				3955

[TD 269]

[Beurla]

[TD 270]

RANN DO ’N GHAIDHLIG ’S DO ’N PHIOB-MHOIR, ’SA’ BHLIADHNA 1781

Tha ’n Comunn Rìoghail Gàidhlig
An tràths’ a’ cumail suas
Cuimhn’ air seòl nan àrmann
A b’ àbhaist bhith ’ga luaidh;
A’ chainnt a dh’ ionnsaich iàdsan dhuibh,			3960
’S i ghnàthaich sibh gu buan;
Ghléidh sibh stoc na cànain,
’S chan fhàilinnich i uainn.

Is sòlasach an cruinneachadh,
Cinn-chinnidh is daoin’-uails’,				3965
Ard mhóralachd nam fineachan
’S gach ionad tha mun cuairt;
Onoir a thaobh nàduir
’Ga gnàthachadh a nuadh,
Gun gléidh sibh pìob mar b’ àbhaist,				3970
Is Gàidhlig ullamh chruaidh.

’S i ’n labhairt bha ’sa’ Ghàrradh,
Dh’ fhàg Adhamh i aig an t-sluagh;
’S i chainnt a bh’ aig na fàidhean
Thug fios Phàrrais dhuinn a nuas;				3975
’S i bhruidheann a bh’ anns an fhàsach,
’N am tràghadh do ’n Mhuir Ruaidh;
’S i nis a measg an àlaich
Tha làthair anns an uair.

’S i ’s binne bhith ’ga h-éisdeachd				3980
Thuirt beul no chuala cluas;
Their Albainn agus Eirinn,
Sasann féin gur mór a luach;

[TD 271]

[Beurla]

[TD 272]

Aon duin’ aig am bi feum oirre
Cha tréig e ì air dhuais;					3985
’S i chùis as fheàrr gun d’ éirich i
An déis dhi bhith ’na suain.

Bu mhór am beud gum bàsaicheadh
A’ chànain as fheàrr buaidh;
’S i ’s treis’ thoirt greis air àbhachd				3990
’S a h-uil’ àit ’n téid a luaidh;
’S i ’s fheàrr gu adhbhar-ghàire,
’S as binne bhlàithe fuaim;
’S i ceòl nam pìob ’s nan clàrsach
Luchd-dàn’ is dhèanamh dhuan.				3995

’S i ’s fheàrr gu togail inntinn
Le binnghuth chòmhradh tlàth;
’S i ’s sgaitiche gu mìomholadh
’S as mìne nochdas gràdh;
’N am cruinneachadh nam mìltean				4000
Le pìob gu iomairt lann,
’S i dhùisgeadh colg air òigridh
’N uair thogte sròl ri crann.

’S i pìob nam feadan siùbhlach
A bhuidhneadh cliù ’sa’ champ,				4005
Air thoiseach nan laoch ùra,
’S meòir lùthmhor dlùth ’nan deann;
A’ chaismeachd ghasda shùnndach,
Bu dùthchas di bhith ann;
’S pailt a nis as ùr i,						4010
Ged bha i aonuair gann.

Le spionnadh chàirdean Gàidhealach
Tha Lunnain làn a nis,
Ag àrdachadh na Gàidhlig
A h-uile là mar thig;						4015
Aig feabhas ’s tha na h-àrmainn
’Ga gnàthachadh gu tric,
B’ e gaol gach duin’ an Sasainn
I bhith aca-san ’nam miosg.

[TD 273]

[Beurla]

[TD 274]

A’ chainnt choibhneil thaitneach				4020
Dheas-labhrach bhlasda bhrisg,
’S lìonmhor cliù tha ’n taice rith’,
Fasan agus mios;
Tha ceòl is Gàidhlig Alba
’S luchd-seanchais ’g a bheil fios				4025
’Gam fòghlam feadh nan Garbhchrioch,
’S ’gan dearbhadh ’san Eaglais Bhric.

[TD 275]

[Beurla]

[TD 276]

RANN DO ’N GHAIDHLIG ’S DO ’N PHIOB-MHOIR ’SA’ BHLIADHNA 1782

Tha ’n Comunn uasal Rìoghail
A’ sìor chur seòil an dràsd
Air nàdurrachd an sìnnsireachd				4030
A thogail cinn ’s gach àit:
A’ Ghàidhlig air a mìneachadh
O ’s cinnteach gur i ’s fheàrr—
An labhairt phrìseil chùramach
Rinn cùmhnanta ri Adhamh.					4035

Tha gach duine ’g ìnnseadh dhuinn,
Cho cinnteach ris a’ bhàs,
Gur i bu chainnt aig Nòah
’N am seòladh anns an àirc,
’S i uaith sin gu lìonmhor					4040
Aig gach lìnnidh a ta fàs;
’S cha téid i chaoidh air dìochuimhn
Gus an tìm an tig am bràth.

Tha Ghàidhlig air a lìonadh
De mhìorbhaile gu léir:					4045
Iùlmhor fonnmhor fàilteachail,
A’ cur a gràdh an céill;
Mire ’s cluich is gàirdeachas,
Is mànran anns gach beul—
Cha chuala sinn an eachdraidh				4050
Na ’s ceairte na i féin.

Tha gach fasan Gàidhealach
An dràsd a’ tighinn gu feum:
Na deisichean a b’ àbhaist dhaibh,
’S a b’ fheàrr leo aca féin;					4055

[TD 277]

[Beurla]

[TD 278]

Coinneamh anns gach àite
Aig na h-àrmainn as fheàrr beus,
Gach duine labhairt Gàidhlig dhiubh,
’S a’ phìob a ghnàth an gleus.

’S i pìob-mhór na h-Eaglais’ Brice				4060
A’ phìob as mò mios an Albainn;
Fàinneachan chnàmh air a dosaibh,
’S i gu làidir socair calma;
Séidear ’na màla an toiseach
Na lìonas a corp le aintheas;					4065
’S sùnndach an ionnsramaid phort i,
Is àrd a chluinnte gloc a sealbhain.

Tha i eireachdail r’ a faicinn,
Chan ’eil ball de ’n acainn cearbach,
Le ribheid nam binnghuth blasda,				4070
’S an stoc dreachmhor air a charbhadh;
Gaothair’ deas dìreach gasda,
Anns na fasanan as fhearr dhiubh;
Sionnsair choimh-lìonadh gach facail
A nì chaisimeachd a dhearbhadh.				4075

Tha i measail air gach banais
A bhitheas am fearann nan Garbhchrioch;
’S feàirrd’ an camp i ’n am dhaibh tarraing,
Gu seinn coimh-theanal na h-armailt;
’S math i g’ an dùsgadh ’sa’ mhadainn,			4080
’S g’ an cur a chadal mu anmoch;
Tha i còrr an am an eadraidh,
’S e ’m feasgar a’ chuid as fhearr dhi.

’S lìonmhor suirghich aig an ainnir
Tha tighinn ceanalta ’na tairgse;				4085
Ge bè aca leis an téid i,
Bithidh eudach ris agus farmad;
Am fear dh’ a bheil an dàn a cosnadh,
’S ann air a ta ’m fortan margaidh—
Iùbhrach nam pongannan glana				4090
’S éibhinn dh’ a leannan bhith falbh leath’.

[TD 279]

[Beurla]

[TD 280]

Tha i measail ann an Lunnainn,
Fhuair i urram anns an tìr seo;
’S feàrr i na torman na clàrsaich,
’S thug i bàrr air cluiche fìdhle;				4095
’S mór an onoir th’ aig a’ phàirtidh,
Nach leig iad gu bràth a dhìth oirnn
Ceòl gun a leithid r’ a àireamh,
’S cànain urramach na fìrinn.

Rogha gach cainnt Gàidhlig ra-mhath,			4100
Tagha gach ciùil sgal na pìoba;
’S ann a nis tha ’n t-am gu tarraing
Aig àrd luchd-ealaidh na rìoghachd,
Le ceòl siùbhlach lùthmhor ealamh
Sùnndach caithriseach luath dìonach;				4105
Tha ’n seo breitheanas air talamh,
’S gheibh gach fear a réir na nì e.

[TD 281]

[Beurla]

[TD 282]

RANN DO ’N GHAIDHLIG ’S DO ’N PHIOB-MHOIR ’SA’ BHLIADHNA 1783

Tha sgeul agam dhuibh r’ a ìnnseadh
Air ceòl ’s air cànain,
A’ toirt cliù air cluiche pìoba					4110
’S air labhairt Gàidhlig,
Tha ’n dràsd a’ cinntinn lìonmhor
’S a h-uil’ àite,
’G àrdachadh onoir na rìoghachd
Anns an d’ fhàs sinn.						4115

’S i th’ aig gach ministeir sgìreachd
’S gach tìr àraidh,
Toirt gu ceart dhuinn eachdraidh Bhìobaill,
An seòl cràbhaidh;
Tha i ’m beul gach filidh, mìneachadh			4120
Ceòl-dàna,
Is i as fheàrr gu moladh prìseil,
’S gu fìor chàineadh.

Tha i cruadalach cruaidh sgairteil
Do dhaoin’-uaisle reachdmhor làidir;				4125
An am treuntais no gaisge,
’S i as deas-fhaclaich’ ’san àit ud;
Tha i ciùin an cùisean fialaidh,
A chur an gnìomh a briathra blàtha;
’S tha i còrr a sgoltadh riasain,				4130
Chum sluagh gun chiall a chur sàmhach.

Tha i iùlmhor fiosrach coibhneil
Freagarrach faighneachdach bàidheil;
’S measail a labhairt ’s a h-éisdeachd
A chur gach deud air fiamh an gàire;				4135

[TD 283]

[Beurla]

[TD 284]

A’ sùgradh ’s a’ bruidhinn le chéile
A’ togail éibhnis mire ’s mànran,
Sìobhalta farasda beusach,
Am beul gach neach a ta nàrach.

Tha Ghàidhlig ’s a’ phìob ag éirigh				4140
Gu mór spéis an tìr nan Gàidheal;
Urram gach ciùil le deagh reusan,
’S ann aig a’ phìob féin a tà e;
’S tormanach pongail a their i
Gach fonn ceileir thig o bràghad;				4145
’S i ’s binne ’s as àird’ a sheinneas,
Cha chluinnear ceòl eile làimh rith’.

’S binn an nuallan ud r’ a éisdeachd
’N uair a chuirear séid ’na màla,
’S a cheartaicheas fear a gleusaidh				4150
Ceart r’ a chéile na duis àrda;
’S cianail a sheinneas i cumha,
’S subhach a sheinneas i fàilte,
Urlar is siubhal gu siùbhlach,
’S crùnludh mum fuirich i sàmhach.				4155

’S e ’n dà chuid i, ceòl is caismeachd,
’S cridheil air astar ’s an tàmh i;
’S bha i riamh air bheul gach caisteil,
Ri dian mhacnas le ceum sràide;
’S leig iad aonuair i a cleachdadh,				4160
Gun bhith ac’ ach an corr àite;
Tha i nis gu grinn am fasan,
’S cinnteach dhi mairsinn gu bràth ann.

Banmhaighstir gach inneal ciùil
A’ phìob ùr seo thàin’ an dràsd oirnn,			4165
A chuireas fir ghleusda gu ’n dùbhlan,
Nach leig dhiùbh gun deuchainn ghàbhaidh;
Fear a buidhne bidh e cliùiteach,
’S onoir dh’ a dhùthaich ’s dh’ a chàirdean,
A’ phìob seo bhith air a ghiùlan,				4170
G’ ar dùsgadh madainn a màireach.

[TD 285]

[Beurla]

[TD 286]

RANN DO ’N GHAIDHLIG ’S DO ’N PHIOB-MHOIR ’SA’ BHLIADHNA 1784

Innsidh mi sgeul àraid dhuibh
Air cànain is air ceòl,
Rogha na deas Ghàidhlig
’S i as fheàrr gu ìnnseadh sgeòil;				4175
A’ chainnt as lìonmhor pàirtean,
’S as mìlse mànran beòil,
Gu freagarrach deas-labhrach,
’S i ardchuiseach gu leòr.

’S i chainnt a bh’ aig na rìghribh				4180
’Gan robh ’n rìoghachd seo ’nan còir;
’S i bruidheann dhiùc is iarlachan,
’S i dh’ iarradh iad mu ’m bòrd;
’S i bh’ aig na daoin’-uaisle,
’S a gheibht’ aig an tuath chòir;				4185
’S i bhà, ’s a thà, aig buachaillean
A’ cuartachadh nam bó.

’N uair a sgaoil na cainntean
Aig tùr aimhreidh mór,
Fhuair a’ Ghàidhlig maighstireachd				4190
’San am sin thar gach seòrs’—
Gur i as fheàrr gu teangaireachd
Tha ’n ceann aon neach tha beò,
Geur soilleir fonnmhor òranach
An seòmraichean an òil.					4195

’S lìonmhor urram làidir
Fhuair a’ Ghàidhlig air gach seòl:
’S i rinn a’ cheud Sàcramaid
Do ’n Phàp a bha ’san Ròimh;

[TD 287]

[Beurla]

[TD 288]

’S i th’ aig cléir an àite seo,					4200
Gach là toirt comhairl’ òirnn;
Gaol filidh is luchd-dàna
Chainnt nàdurra gun ghò.

’S i fhuair sinn o na pàranta
A rinn ar n-àrach òg;						4205
’S i bu mhath leinn fhàgail
Aig an àl tha teachd òirnn;
Tha h-uile car a dh’ ìnnsinn oirr’
A’ cur a prìs am mòid,
Gur i cainnt as brìoghmhoire,					4210
’S ì phìob as fheàrr gu ceòl.

A’ phìob ùr seo thàinig do ’n bhaile
A dh’ fhaotainn urram,
’S i ceann inneal-ciùil an fhearainn,
’S na dùthch’ uile;						4215
Le meòir lùthmhor air a crannaibh,
’S le dlùth bhuillean,
’S àrd a chluinnt’ i, ’s binn a langan,
’S grinn a cumachd.

Tha dosan le ìobhraidh ballach,				4220
Cochull de ’n t-sìoda m’ a muineal;
’S osgarra dìonach a callan
Air thoiseach mhìltean air thurus;
Brosnachadh rìoghail na carraid
An cabhaig, an strìth no ’n cumasg;				4225
Cha bhi sproc ’san tìr am fan i,
’S fortanach an tì dh’ am buin i.

’S deò-gréine leis an luchd-ealaidh
Tha ’n Albainn gu léir ’s an Lunnainn,
A’ phìob as math gleus is gearradh,				4230
Làidir fallain eutrom ullamh;
’S mór an t-éibhneas i dh’ a leannan
Bhith aige ’na sgéith ’ga cumail:
Fonn-cheòl réidh a cré na h-ainnir,
Beusan glana na treun chulaidh.				4235

[TD 289]

[Beurla]

[TD 290]

’S e cheud cheòl a bh’ air an talamh
A’ phìob-mhór as bòidhche guileag;
’S i bh’ aig Fionn, aig Goll ’s aig Garadh,
Ann an talla nan laoch fuileach;
’S mairg a chitheadh air seòl calla				4240
Caismeachd chaithriseach nan curaidh;
Mhosgladh i le séid dh’ a h-anail,
Gu feum ealamh, an Fhéinn uile.

Mu ghibht phrìseil gun a ceannach,
Tha ’n coimh-theanal seo air chumail;			4245
Breitheachan dìleas ’gan tarraing,
A nì ceart an fhìrinn uile;
Gheibh gach fear a réir na h-ealaidh
Anns am bi e fhéin ’na urrainn;
’S tha e saor aig math-an-airidh				4250
A’ phìob fhaotainn thar gach duine.

[TD 291]

[Beurla]

[TD 292]

RANN DO ’N GHAIDHLIG ’S DO ’N PHIOB-MHOIR ’SA’ BHLIADHNA 1785

Seo cruinneachadh uaislean miosail
Tha a’ cumail suas am fasan
Na cainnt a tha buadhmhor fiosrach
Le ’m fìor bhrisg a chualas eachdraidh;			4255
Tha i luath ’s chan ’eil i liotach,
’S tha i cruaidh ma labhrar ceart i,
’S chan ’eil a luchd-fuatha bitheant’,
’S i bha tric aig luchd nam breacan.

Cànain gun truailleadh gun mhiosgadh			4260
’S Gàidheil dh’ an dual i bhith aca;
’S nàdurra dh’ a fuaim bhith miosail,
’S misneachail an sluagh a chleachd i;
Cainnt mhàthaireil gun bhruaidlean idir,
Ach bhith làn de shuairceas tlachdmhor;			4265
Ceòl-gàire ’ga luaidh gu bitheant’
’S luchd-dàna ’ga luath chur seachad.

Tha Lunnainn glé àrd am misnich
Le spionnadh nan Gàidheal gasda
Fhuair urram ’s gach àit an sirt’ iad,				4270
Na curaidhean calma reachdmhor,
A tha gabhail cùram riochdail
A chumail na rìoghachd neartmhor,
’S dh’ òrdaich gu sìorraidh nach brisear
Gàidhlig, pìobaireachd is bratach.				4275

Tha uaislean Dhùn Eideann le gliocas
Gu rìoghail réidhbheartach tlachdmhor;
Chan fheud eucoir bhith ’nam miosg-san,
’S ann dhaibh féin as léir an ceartas;

[TD 293]

[Beurla]

[TD 294]

Ris an fheumach tha iad iochdmhor,				4280
’S air na béistean tha iad smachdail;
An am treubhantais no trioblaid,
’S mairg a theannadh ri leum tharta.

Có theannadh ri leum thairis
Air na laochaibh fearail treubhach,				4285
Na Gàidheil àrdanach uaibhreach,
’S iad làidir ri guaillibh a chéile;
A chuireadh crith air càch le fuathas
An am bhualadh nan lann geura?
’S mairg air an cromadh na tuathaich,			4290
Comunn cruadaladh nach géilleadh.

Tha gach car tha tighinn mun cuairt dhaibh
An tràths’ na’s buadhmhoire na chéile:
Am fearann a chaidh a thoirt uatha,
Gun d’ fhuair iad uile gu léir e;				4295
Bidh gach dligheach far ’m bu dual dhaibh,
’S uachdarain air an cuid féin iad;
Bithidh na h-oighreachan suas dheth,
’S cha bhi tuathanach ’na éigin.

’N uair sheallas sinn air ar fallaing				4300
Bheir sinn beannachd air a’ Ghreumach,
’S air Mac Shimidh mór na Mormhaich,
Am mormhair a bu mhath feum dhuinn;
’Sa’ chùirt a b’ àirde bha ’n Lunnainn
Fhuair iad ann urram is éisdeachd,				4305
’S tha ’n rìoghachd uile ’nan comain—
Fhuair iad dhuinn comas ar n-éididh.

Tha coimh-thional rìoghail Ghàidheal
An tràth-s’ am baile Dhùn Eideann,
A’ cumail am prìs na Gàidhlig				4310
A thaobh nàduir os cionn Beurla,
’S a’ gleidheadh pìob-mhór mar b’ àbhaist
Os cionn clàrsaich no ceòl theudan,
’S an dà thoil-inntinn sin fhàgail
Aig an àlach thig ’nar déidh-ne.				4315

[TD 295]

[Beurla]

[TD 296]

RANN DO ’N GHAIDHLIG ’S DO ’N PHIOB-MHOIR ’SA’ BHLIADHNA 1789

Brosnachadh cluiche na pìoba
Dh’ ìnnsinn pàirt deth:
An toiseach a gleusadh ’n uair a lìonar
Séid ’na màla;
Fonnmhor freagarrach dh’ a chéile				4320
Na duis àrda,
Làn toil-inntinn do ’n luchd-éisdeachd
Bhios ’ga clàistinn.

Pìob uallach nam maidean réidhe
’S nan ceanna cnàmha,					4325
De ’n fhiodh chruaidh thig a Semeuca,
’S fheàrr tha fàs ann,
Air a thuairneireachd cruinn dìreach,
Iobhaireach fàinneach;
Gaothaireach feadanach fìnealt’				4330
Le binne chàileachd.

’S freagarrach a’ chuid a steach dhith,
’S tha ’n taobh mach dhith dreachmhor dàicheil,
Tonnagach ruibeineach rìomhach,
Dosan de ’n t-sìoda ri srannraich,				4335
Mu mhuineal nam buaidhean prìseil
Cumail dìon air a mìn bhràghad;
Cuilc ’na slugan tha ’ga lìonadh,
Air a dhìonachadh le snàithean.

’S i phìob ùr a tha ’n Dùn Eideann				4340
Eibhneas Ghàidheal,
Inneal-ciùil as fheàrr fo ’n ghréin,
Le reusan àraid:

[TD 297]

[Beurla]

[TD 298]

Tha i snasmhor maiseach fìnealt’
Cuimir dreachmhor dìonach làidir,				4345
Gu binn bòidheach seòcail ceutach
Ceòlmhor eutrom éibhinn àlainn.

Pìob a chuireadh sunnd gu mire,
Fonn is faram,
Air gach diùc is àrd cheann-cinnidh				4350
’S oighre fearainn;
Bidh gach duin’-uasal ’ga sireadh
Gu togail a shluaigh ’sa’ charraid,
’N am tharraing a suas gach fine
Dhol a bhualadh nan cruaidh lannan.				4355

Ceòl as rìoghaile ’s as sine
Chuala sinne bhith air thalamh,
Ceòl as brìoghmhoire ’s as binne
’S as grinne thug meòir a crannaibh;
Cha chualas neach riamh a dhiomoil				4360
Dreach is dèanadas na h-ainnir,
’S fhuair i cliù le beul gach filidh
A bha ’s dùthaich b’ fhiach gu rannan.

Tha ’n rìoghachd làn éibhnis uile
’S Dùn Eideann gu tric ’nan aire,				4365
Liuthad treunfhear th’ ann a’ cumail
Reachd is reusan a’ choimh-theanail:
Cainnt as géire chuala duine,
’S urramach gach beul a chanas
A’ chànain a ta réidh ullamh					4370
Beusach furanach, glé ealamh.

’S onoir do ’n Ghàidhealtachd turus
Na thàinig an dràsd do ’n bhaile,
Chumail am prìs brìgh an t-seanchais
Tha farmadach leis na Gallaibh;				4375
Gàidhlig Albannach nan curaidh,
’S a’ phìob, banmhaighstir gach ealaidh,
An ceòl ’s a’ chainnt a fhuair gach urram,
’S luaithe bh’ ann ’s as fhaide mhaireas.

[TD 299]

[Beurla]

[TD 300]

RAINN DO ’N PHADHADH

’S bochd an deireadh beatha bròn,				4380
’S olc an deireadh òil padhadh;
’S muladach suidhe mu ’n bhòrd
Gun an stòp a lìonadh fhathast;
’S aighearach daoin’-uaisle còir
Aig a bheil stòras ’nan lamhan,				4385
Nì òl ’n uair bhios iad pàiteach,
’S a bheir pàigheadh do na mnathan.

’S éibhinn ’sa’ mhadainn a’ chòmhdhail
Thighinn òirnne toiseach an latha—
Bean-uasal a’ tighinn g’ a seòmar				4390
A chur sòlas feadh an taighe;
Botal mór aice ’na làimh,
’S e dear-làn a dh’ uisge beatha;
’S òl gu cridheil air a chéile
’S their i fhéin gur e ar beatha.				4395

’S e fasan ceart a’s taigh-thàirne
Misneach àrd ’san am gu caitheamh;
Bidh fear leis nach toil am branndaidh
Ri cùl-chainnt oirnn chionn a ghabhail;
’S e their companach a’ bhotail,				4400
“Lìon a suas an copan fathast;
’S mór na mhaoidheas orm mo dheoch,
Ach ’s beag na dh’ fhidireas mo phadhadh.”

[TD 301]

[Beurla]

[TD 302]

ORAN A’ BHRANNDAIDH

Di-haal-lum, di-haal-lum, di-i’il i’il, hanndan,
Di-dir-ir-i-hal-hi’il-lum, di-dir-ir-i-hal-haoi-rum;		4405
Di-i’il-i’il-hal-dir-ir-i, ha-ri-ha’al-haoi-rum,
Di-i’il-haal-dil-il-i’il, dor-ri-ho’ol-hann-dan.

Tha fortan ann, bidh deoch againn,
Na biodh an copan gann oirnn;
Tha pailteas anns na botalaibh,				4410
Chan ’eil an stoc air chall oirnn;
Is feàirrde sinn an toiseach e
Gu brosnachadh ar cainnte;
Ged bhiodh a h-uile deoch againn
’S e ’s docha leinn am branndaidh.				4415
Di-haal-lum, di-haal-lum, &c.

’S e sin an sruthan mireanach,
An tobar milis seannsail;
Tha binneas mar ri grinneas
A chur spioraid am fear fann ann;				4420
Is feàirrde sinn na shireas sinn,
Cha chulaidh mhilleadh cheann e;
’S ro-mhath an seise muineil
Do gach duine ghabhas rann e.

Na fir anns a bheil cridhealas,					4425
Nach ’eil an cridhe gann ac’,
Companaich na dighe,
A nì suidhe leis an dram iad;
Iarraidh iad a rithist e
Ma bhitheas beagan ann deth;					4430
’N uair chluinneas iad an fhidheall
Bidh iad fioghaireach gu dannsadh.

[TD 303]

[Beurla]

[TD 304]

’N uair gheibh sinn de na baraillean
Na ’s math leinn fo ’r comannda,
Na cupain a tha falamh					4435
Bhith le searraig a’ cur annta,
Gach caraid bhios a’ taitneadh ruinn
Gum b’ ait leinn e bhith cainnt ruinn,
’N uair thig a’ ghlaine bhasdalach
Air bhlas an t-siùcair-channdaidh.				4440

Cha chunnart duinn e theireachdainn,
Tha seileir anns an Fhraing dheth;
Chan ’eil eagal gainne
Air an loingeas thug a nall e;
Their sinne, on bu toigh leinn e,				4445
Nach dèan a choire call oirnn,
Air fhad ’s gun dèan sinn fuireach ris,
Bhith gabhail tuilleadh sannt ait.

Na fir a tha ’nan sgrubairean,
Nach caith an cuid ’san am seo,				4450
Chan imir iad bhith cuide ruinn
’Nan tubaistean le ganntar;
Cha sir iad dol an cuideachd,
Is chan iarr a’ chuideachd ann iad;
Mur cuir am bùrn am padhadh dhiubh,			4455
Chan fhaigheadh iad am branndaidh.

[TD 305]

[Beurla]

[TD 306]

ORAN A’ BHOTAIL

’N uair a shuidheas sinn socair
’S a dh’ òlas sinn botal,
Chan aithnich ar stoc uainn
Na chuireas sinn ann;						4460
Thig onoir is fortan
Le sonas a’ chopain,
C’ar son nach bi deoch oirnn
Mun tog sinn ar ceann?
Bheir an stuth grinn oirnn					4465
Seinn gu fileanta,
Chuir a thoil-inntinn
Binneas ’nar cainnt;
Chaisg i ar n-ìota
’N fhìor dheoch mhilis,					4470
Bu mhuladach sinne
Nam biodh i air chall.

Deoch-slàinte nan gaisgeach,
Nan Gàidhealaibh gasda,
Dh’ am b’ àbhaist mar fhasan					4475
Bhith pòit air an dram;
Luchd-gaoil an stuth bhlasda,
’S air dhaoiread an lacha,
Nach caomhnadh am beartas
A sgapadh ’san am.						4480
Fear ’g a bheil nì
Gheibh e na shireas e,
Fear a tha crìonda
Fanadh e thall;
Fear a tha mìodhoir						4485
Chan fhuiling sinn’ e,
’S am fear a bheil grinneas
Théid iomain a nall.

[TD 307]

[Beurla]

[TD 308]

’S ro-rìoghail an obair
Sruth brìoghmhor na togalach,				4490
Iocshlaint a bhogaicheas
Cridhe tha gann;
’S e chuireadh an sodan
Air fear a bhiodh togarrach,
’S chuireadh e ’m bodach					4495
A fear a bhiodh teann.
Chan ’eil ’san tìr
Uasal no cumanta
Nach ’eil air thì
Gach urram a th’ ann;						4500
Ged a bhiodh strìth
Mu thogail na muirichinn,
Cia mar as urrainn sinn
Fuireach o ’n dram?

Tha e fionnar do ’n chreubhaig				4505
A h-uile là gréine
Thig teas o na speura
Thar sléibhte nam beann;
’S e math ri là reòdhta
Chur blàths ann am pòra					4510
An fhir théid dh’ a dheòin
An taigh-òsda ’na dheann.
Cuiridh e sùnnd
Air muinntir eireachdail,
Timcheall a’ bhùird,						4515
’S cuid eile dhiubh danns’;
Thogamaid fonn neo-throm
Is ceileirean,
’S freagarrach sheinneas sinn
Deireadh gach rann.						4520

On shuidh sinn cho fada,
’S a dh’ òl sinn na bh’ againn,
’S i chòir dol a chadal
On thàinig an t-am;

[TD 309]

[Beurla]

[TD 310]

Chan fhóghnadh ach pailteas					4525
Thoirt sòlas dh’ ar n-aigneadh,
Deoch mhór anns a’ mhadainn
Gu leigheas ar ceann.
Am fear tha gun chlì
Cuiridh e spiorad ann,						4530
Togaidh e crìdh’
Gach fir a tha fann;
Théid am fear tinn
Gu grinn air mhire:
’S e leigheas gach tinnis					4535
Deoch mhilis an dram.

[TD 311]

[Beurla]

[TD 312]

ORAN ALASDAIR

Alasdair nan stòp ann an Sràid a’ Chùil,
Sin an duine còir air a bheil mo rùn;
Alasdair nan stòp ann an Sràid a’ Chùil.

’S coma leat an siola						4540
B’ annsa leat an stòp;
Chan e sin bu docha
Ach am botal mór.
Alasdair nan stòp, &c.

Théid thu do ’n taigh-òsda					4545
’S òlaidh tu gu fial;
Cha robh gainne stòrais
Air do phòca riamh.

Bha thu greis ad aimsir
Ann an arm an Rìgh;						4550
Cumaidh sin riut airgead,
’S fhearra dhuit e na nì.

Gheibheadh tu le d’ cheanal
Leannan anns gach tìr;
Ged a bhiodh tu falamh					4555
Cha bhiodh bean ad dhìth.

Tha thu math air fairge,
’S tric thu marbhadh éisg;
Cas a shiubhal garbhlaich,
Théid thu shealg an fhéidh.					4560

Ged thuirt Calum breac
Nach robh thu tapaidh riamh,
Có a chreideadh sin
Ach duine bha gun chiall?

[TD 313]

[Beurla]

[TD 314]

’N uair a théid mi Ghlaschu					4565
’S taitneach leam bhith ’g òl
Ann an taigh mo charaid,
Alasdair nan stòp.

[TD 315]

[Beurla]

[TD 316]

AOIR UISDEIN

Turus a chaidh mi air astar
A Chinn t-Sàile,						4570
Chunna’ mi daoin’-uaisle tlachdmhor
Coibhneil pàirteach;
Bha aon bhalach ann air banais
A thug dhomh tàmailt:
On bha esan mar sin dòmh-sa					4575
Bidh mise mar seo dhà-san.

’S ann an sin a thòisich Uisdean,
Mar a nì cù an droch nàduir,
Tabhannaich ri sluagh na dùthcha
’S b’ e rùn gun gearradh e ’n sàiltean;			4580
’S math an companach do ’n chù e,
’S dona ’n companach le càch e;
Cha chuideachd e bhàrd no phìobair’
Aig a’ mhìomhalachd ’s a dh’ fhàs e.

Aidich fhéin nach ’eil thu ’d phìobair’,			4585
’S leig dhìot bhith ’m barail gur bàrd thu:
Daoine cridheil iad le chéile,
’S bithidh iad gu léir a’ tàir ort;
Fear-ciùil gun bhinneas gun ghrinneas,
Fuadaichidh sinn as ar pàirt e,					4590
Mar a thilgeas iad craobh chrìonaich
O ’n fhìonain a mach as a’ ghàrradh.

Ma chì thusa bàrd no filidh
No fear-dàna,
Ma bhios aon diubh ’g iarraidh gille				4595
Ghiùlan màileid,
Lean an duine sin le dùrachd
Los gun siùbhladh tu h-uil’ àite;
’S mór an glanadh air do dhùthaich
I chur cùl riut ’s thu dh’ a fàgail.				4600

[TD 317]

[Beurla]

[TD 318]

No ma chì thu fear a sheinneas
Pìob no clàrsach,
Feudaidh tusa ’n t-inneal-ciùil
A ghiùlan dà-san,
Gus am bi craiceann do dhroma				4605
Fàs na bhallaibh loma bàna,
Mar a chì thu milleadh srathrach
Air gearran a bhios ri àiteach.

Cia mar a dhèanadh e òran
Gun eòlas gun tuigse nàduir?					4610
O nach dèanadh e air dòigh e
Bu chòra dha fuireach sàmhach;
Bruidhinn ghlugach ’s cuid dith mabach,
Móran stadaich ann am pàirt dith;
Na nì e phlabairtich chòmhraidh,				4615
Cha bheò na thuigeas a Ghàidhlig.

Sgimilear cheanna nam bòrd thu
Far am faigh thu ’n t-òl gun phàigheadh;
Cia mar chunntas sinn na geòcaich
Mur bi Uisdean òg ’san àireamh?				4620
Cha robh do bhrù riamh aig sìochaimh
Gus an lìonadh tu bhiadh chàich i;
’S mór an tolc na chaisgeadh t’ ìotadh,
’N uair a chìt’ thu ’s do ghloc pàiteach.

’S tric do leaba ’n lag an òtraich,				4625
No ’n cùl gàrraidh;
Bidh do cheann air conntom còmhnard,
’S ro-mhath ’n t-àit e;
Bidh na coin ag imlich t’ fheòsaig
A’ toirt dìot a’ bheòil ’s a’ chàirein,				4630
Do chraos dreamach toirt phòg salach
Do d’ dhearbh-bhràithrean.

[TD 319]

[Beurla]

[TD 320]

Nan cluinneadh sibh muc a’ rùcail,
Geòidh is tunnagan a’ ràcail,
’S ann mar sin a bha pìob Uisdein				4635
Brònach muladach a’ rànaich;
Muineal gun aolmann air tùchadh,
’N ribheid chan fhaod a bhith làidir,
’S e call daonnan air a chùlaibh
Na gaoith bu chòir dol ’sa’ mhàla.				4640

Bha lurga coin air son gaothair’
Ad chraos farsaing,
’S culaidh sin a thogail plàigh’
’S an cnàimh air malcadh;
Rinn e t’ anail salach breun,					4645
Ma théid neach fo ’n ghréin an taic riut,
’S fheàrr bhith eadar thu ’s a’ ghaoth
Na seasamh air taobh an fhasgaidh.

Cia mar a nì Uisdean òg dhuibh
Ceòl gu dannsa,						4650
’N uair a chitheadh tu sruth ronn
O ’n h-uile toll a bh’ air an t-seannsair?
Sgeul tha fìor a dh’ ìnnseas mise,
Gur h-e dh’ fhàg e nis cho manntach,
Gun tug iad dheth leis an t-siosar				4655
Bàrr na teanga.

Séididh Uisdean pìob an rongain,
’S mór a h-anntlachd;
Bidh i cosmhail ri gaoir choinnspeach
A bhiodh an cnoc fraoich a’ dranndail;			4660
An Circepoll làimh ri Tunga,
A’ baigearachd air muinntir bainnse,
Fhuair mise pìobaire ’n rumpaill
’S dh’ fhàg mi ann e.

[TD 321]

[Beurla]

[TD 322]

AOIR ANNA

Anna nighean Uilleim an Cromba,				4665
Bean gun chonn ’s i fhéin air aimhreadh,
’N uair chaidh mi ’n toiseach g’ a sealltainn
Chan e ’m fortan a chuir ann mi;
Bhruidhinn mise sàmhach socair,
Mar dhuine bochd ag iarraidh fàrdaich;			4670
Thòisich ise mar chù crosda
Bhiodh anns na dorsan a’ dranndail.

’S ann aice tha beul na sgallais
Gu fanaid a dhèanamh air seann-duin’
Nach urrainn a dhèanamh feum dhi				4675
Mar a bha i féin an geall air;
Chunna’ mise latha ghluaisinn
Leis na gruagaichean mar chairdeas;
Dh’ aithnich i gun d’ fhalbh an uair sin,
’S chuir i uaithe mi le angar.					4680

Innsidh mi dhuibh teisneas Anna
On as aithne dhomh ’san am i:
Bean a dh’ òl a peighinn-phisich,
Cha bheò idir gun an dram i;
Cha neònach leam i bhith misgeach,				4685
’S i ’n còmhnaidh a miosg a’ bhranndaidh;
’S tric a bha ’na broinn a leòr dheth,
’S bha tuilleadh ’s a’ chòir ’na ceann deth.

Chan ’eil a leannan r’ a fhaicinn
Ach fear m’ a seach de na ceàrdaibh;				4690
’S e ’n onoir as motha th’ aice
Gum fairtlich i air na bàrdaibh;

[TD 323]

[Beurla]

[TD 324]

Thug i dhìom am beul ’s an t-sròn,
On dh’ fhàg i beò mi tha mi taingeil;
Chuir i mise sàmhach balbh,					4695
’S dh’ fhalbh mi mun tugadh i ’n ceann dìom.

’S mór an treuntas le Anna
Bhith cho geur le sgainneal chainnte;
’S mairg air ’n a thachair bean bheumnach
Aig a bheil am beul gun fhaithmeadh.			4700
Am fear a bheir ise dhachaigh
’S ann air thig a’ chreach ’s an calldach;
’N uair shaoil e gum bu bhean cheart i,
’S ann thachair e ri bhan-mhaighstir.

A’ bhan-chleasaiche gun ghrinneas,				4705
’S mairg fleasgach a théid ’na caraibh;
’S tric i tuiteam leis na gillean,
Ceap-tuislidh i do na fearaibh;
A’ bhean bhruidhneach mhisgeach ghionach
Ghleadhrach lonach shanntach shalach,			4710
Rinn gu reubadh air a teangaidh,
Cosmhail ri gath geur na nathrach.

Còmhdach nach falaich a craiceann,
Leòmach gun seòl air cur leis ann;
Chan ’eil brògan slàn m’ a casan,				4715
Chan ’eil còta ’n àird m’a leasan;
Oirre tha aogasg na glaistig,
Neul an aoig ’na h-aodann preasach;
Closach i air seargadh, lachdann,
’S cosmhail i ri dealbh na leisge.				4720

Taigh tha làn de mhnathan misgeach,
’S olc an t-àit an d’ rinn mi tachairt;
Ged thàinig mi ann gun fhios domh,
’S fheàrr falbh tràth na fuireach aca.
Banmhaighstir a’ chomuinn bhristich,			4725
Anna tha ainmeil ’san eachdraidh;
Ma gheibh càch i mar fhuair mis’ i,
Cha tig iad gu bràth g’ a faicinn.

[TD 325]

[Beurla]

[TD 326]

CUMHA IARLA BHRAGHAID-ALBANN

’S truagh r’ a éisdeachd an sgeul
Fhuair mi fhéin tuilleadh ’s luath:				4730
Rinn an t-eug ceann na céille
’S nam beus a thoirt uainn;
Chan ’eil léigh tha fo ’n ghréin
Dhèanadh feum dhuit ’san uair;
’S bochd ad dhéidh sinn gu léir,				4735
’S chan ’eil feum bhith ’ga luaidh.

Tha do chàirdean làidir lìonmhor,
Anns gach tìr a tha mun cuairt;
Seo na dh’ fhàg an aigneadh ìosal
Do chorp prìseil bhith ’san uaigh;				4740
’S iad mar loingeas gun bhith dìonach,
Fad o thìr air druim a’ chuain;
’S tusa b’ urrainn an toirt sàbhailt’
Ged a bhiodh an gàbhadh cruaidh.

’S ann an diugh a chaidh do chàradh				4745
An ciste chlàr ’san leabaidh fhuair;
Is muladach ad dhéidh an tràth-s’
A’ chuid as àirde de d’ dhaoin’-uaisl’;
Tha gach duin’ agad fo phràmh,
’S goirt an càs a bheil an tuath;				4750
’S iad do bhochdan a tha cràiteach,
Thugadh an taic làidir uath’.

’S iomadh dìlleachdan òg falamh
Bha le h-ainnis air dhroch shnuadh,
Seann daoine ’s bantraichean fanna				4755
Bha faotainn beathachaidh uait;

[TD 327]

[Beurla]

[TD 328]

’S ann bu truagh a’ ghaoir a bh’ aca,
’S deòir gu frasach air an gruaidh,
Caoineadh cruaidh is bualadh bhasan,
’S bhith toirt pàirt d’ am falt a nuas.				4760

’S muladach an nochd do dhùthaich,
’S dubhach tùirseach tha do shluagh;
Chan iongnadh sin, ’s mór an diùbhail
An tionndadh seo thighinn oirnn cho luath;
Am fear a b’ àbhaist bhith le dùrachd				4765
Gabhail cùram dhiubh gach uair,
Dh’ fhàg iad ’na laighe ’san ùir e
Far nach dùisg e gu là Luain.

’S ann an tràthaibh na Féill Brìghde
Thàinig crìoch air saoi nam buadh;				4770
’S lom a thug an t-eug an sgrìob oirnn,
Och mo dhìth, cha deic a luaths!
Bhuail an gath air flath na fìrinn
Bha ’gar dìonadh o gach cruas;
’S goirid leinn do ré ’san àite,					4775
Ged their càch gun robh thu buan.

Cha do sheall thu riamh gu h-ìosal
Air nì chuireadh sìos an tuath;
Bu chùl-taic dhaibh anns gach àit thu,
’S tu bha ghnàth ’gan cumail suas;				4780
Cha bu mhiann leat togail ùnlaigh,
Sin a’ chùis d’ an tug thu fuath;
Bha thu faotainn gaoil gach duine,
’S ghléidh thu ’n t-urram sin a fhuair.

Bha thu léirsinneach le suairceas,				4785
Dh’ fhàs ad chom an uaisle mhór,
Ciall is misneach mar ri cruadal,
Fhuair thu ’n dualchas sin o d’ sheòrs’;
Bha thu fiosrach glic neo-luaineach,
Bha t’ inntinn buan anns a’ chòir;				4790
On thug iad air ghiùlan sluaigh thu,
’S adhbhar sin a luathaich deòir.

[TD 329]

[Beurla]

[TD 330]

Chan ’eil éibhneas ann am Bealach,
Chan ’eil faram ann no ceòl;
Daoine dubhach, ’s mnathan galach,				4795
’S iad gun ealaidh ach am bròn,
On a chaidh do ghiùlan dachaigh
O ’n Mhachair air mhùthadh seòil—
’N àit an éididh sin a chleachd thu,
Ciste ’s léine ’s brat de ’n t-sròl.				4800

Nam bu daoine bheireadh dhìnn thu,
Dh’ éireadh mìltean air an tòir,
O bheul Tatha gu Latharn Iochdrach—
Sin fo chìs duit agus còrr,
Far an d’ fhàs na gallain fhìorghlan—			4805
Is iad lìonmhor ann gu leòr,
A rachadh togarrach gu d’ dhìoladh,
Nach obadh dol sìos le deòin.

’S ann tha chùis na ’s fheàrr mar thà i,
Dòchas làidir thu bhith beò					4810
A measg nan aingeal a tha ’m Phàrras,
Ann an gàirdeachas ro-mhór;
Gur e ’n Tì a ghlac air làimh thu
Thug ’san àite sin dhuit còir
Air oighreachd as fheàrr na dh’ fhàg thu,			4815
An àros àdhmhor Rìgh na glòir.

Ged tha ’m fear a thig ad àite
Thall an tràths’ thar chuantan mór’,
Guidheam dlùth gun tig e sàbhailt’,
Soirbheas àrd ri cùl gach seòil,				4820
A dh’ fhaotainn seilbh air an t-saidhbhreas
’S air an oighreachd sin bu chòir;
A ghabhail cùram dh’ a chuid fearainn
’S dh’ a chuid daoine, sean is òg.

[TD 331]

[Beurla]

[TD 332]

RAINN I CHALUIM CHILLE

Beannachd I Chaluim Chille—				4825
Innis tha beannaichte cheana,
Eilean a tha ’n ìochdar Mhuile
’S e uile fo chìs Mhic Cailein;
Ionad naomha a fhuair urram
Os cionn iomad tìr is fearann,					4830
Ghabhas dìleas ris gach duine
Thig o ’n uile rìoghachd aineoil.

’S iomad rìgh a th’ anns an tulaich
’S daoin’-uaisle rìomhach a bharrachd,
’S an cuirp phrìseil bu mhath cumachd			4835
Air an leagail sìos fo ’n talamh;
O ’s e deireadh crìch gach duine
Tuiteam ’nan ùir ’s ’nam mìn ghaineamh;
Mo dhòchas an Crìosd a dh’ fhuiling,
Gun d’ ullaich e sìth d’ an anam.				4840

Mìle is dà chiad d’ a thuilleadh
De bhliadhnachan air dol thairis,
On a shuidhich a’ cheud duine
Deagh chlach-bhunaidh stéidh a’ bhalla;
’S iomad dealbh a th’ ann a’ fuireach,			4845
’S leacannan-mharbh air dheagh ghearradh,
Clach shnaidhte o ’n bhlàr gu mhullach,
’S rinn iad uil’ e làidir fallain.

Fhuair sinn searmoin shoilleir ullamh
O ’n fhear a bha ’n dé ’sa’ chrannaig;				4850
’S chuala mi ’n luchd-éisdeachd uile
Toirt urram do ’n bheul a chan i.

[TD 333]

[Beurla]

[TD 334]

Nis on a dh’ eug Calum Cille,
’S nach bu dù dha féin bhith maireann,
Tha aoibhneas air dùthaich Mhuile				4855
Dùghall a bhith ’n àite Chaluim.

[TD 336]

RAINN COMH-DHUNAIDH

Tha mis’ am shuidh’ air an uaigh,
Tha ’n leaba sin fuar gu leòr,
Gun fhios agam cia fhaid’ an tìm
Gus an teannar mi fhìn d’ a còir;				4860
Còmhdach flanainn ’s léine lìn,
Is ciste dhubh dhìonach bhòrd:
Air mheud ’s gun cruinnich mi nì,
Siud na théid leam sìos fo ’n fhòid.

Is beag ar cùram roimh ’n bhàs				4865
’M fad a bhios sinn làidir òg;
Saoilidh sinn ma gheibh sinn dàil,
Gur h-e ar n-àite fuireach beò;
Feudaidh sinn fhaicinn air càch,
’S iad ’gar fàgail gach aon lò,					4870
Gur nàdurra dhuinne gach tràth
Gu bheil am bàs a’ teannadh òirnn.

Tha mo pheacadh-sa ro-throm,
’S muladach sin leam an dràsd;
Tha mi smaoineachadh gu tric				4875
Liuthad uair a bhrist mi ’n àithn’,
Le miann mo dhroch inntinn féin
Leis an robh mo chreubhag làn,
Gun chuimhn’ air ùghdarras Dhé
Le dùrachd am bheul no ’m làimh.				4880

Ged as mór mo pheacadh gnìomh’,
’S mi ’n cionta ciad pheacaidh Adhamh,
Cheannaicheadh mi le fuil gu daor
A dhòirteadh sgaoilteach air a’ bhlàr;
Tha mo dhùil, ’s cha dòchas faoin,				4885
Ri iochd fhaotainn air a sgàth;
Gun glacar m’ anam gu sìth
Le fulangas Chrìosd a mhàin.

[TD 337]

[Beurla]

[TD 338]

Tha mo dhòchas ann an Crìosd
Nach dìobair e mi gu bràth;					4890
’N uair a leagar mo chorp a sìos
Ann an staid ìosail fo ’n bhlàr,
Gun togar m’ anam a suas
Gu rìoghachd nam buadh ’s nan gràs;
Gum bi mo leaba fo dhìon					4895
Cois cathrach an Tì as àird’.

Cha bhiodh m’ eagal roimh an aog,
Ged thigeadh e ’m thaobh gun dàil,
Nam bithinn de pheacadh saor
An déis a’ ghaoil a thug mi dhà;				4900
Tha mo dhùil anns an Dia bheò
Gun dèan e tròcair orm an dràsd,
Mo thoirt a steach a dh’ ionad naomh
’N cuideachd Mhaois is Abrahàm.

Gabhaidh mi nis mo chead de ’n t-sluagh,			4905
Làn toirt suas daibh ann am chainnt,
Fàgaidh mi aca na chnuasaich
Na stuaghan a bh’ ann am cheann,
Los gun abair iad r’ a chéile,
“Mura leugh sinn fhéin gach rann,				4910
Có air an téid sinn g’ an sireadh,
Nis chan ’eil am filidh ann?”

[TD 340]

ORAN DHUN EIDEANN

’S e baile mór Dhùn Eideann
A b’ éibhinn leam bhith ann,
Aite fialaidh farsaing						4915
A bha tlachdmhor anns gach ball;
Gearasdain is batraidh
Is rampairean gu teann,
Taighean móra ’s caisteal
Anns an tric an d’ stad an camp.				4920

’S tric a bha camp rìoghail ann,
’S bu rìomhach an luchd-dreuchd,
Trùp nan srann-each lìonmhor
Gu dìleas air a’ gheàrd;
Bhiodh gach fear cho eòlach					4925
’S a h-uile seòl a b’ fheàrr,
Na fleasgaich bu mhath fòghlam
A dhol an òrdugh blàir.

’S iomadh fleasgach uasal ann
A bha gu suairce grinn,					4930
Fùdar air an gruagan
A suas gu bàrr an cinn;
Leadain dhonna dhualach
’Na chuachagan air snìomh,
Bàrr dosach mar an sìoda					4935
’N uair shlìogadh e le cìr.

’S mór a tha de bhaintighearnan
A null ’s a nall an t-sràid,
Gùntaichean de ’n t-sìoda orr’
’Gan slìogadh ris a’ bhlàr;					4940
Staidhs air na h-ainnirean
’Gan teannachadh gu h-àrd,
Buill-mhais’ air aodainn bhòidheach,
Mar thuilleadh spòrsa dhaibh.

[TD 341]

[Beurla]

[TD 342]

A h-uile té mar thigeadh dhi					4945
Gu miosail a measg chàich,
Uallach rìomhach ruibeineach
Cruinn mìn geal giobach tlàth;
Trusgan air na h-òigheanan
’Gan còmhdachadh gu làr,					4950
Bròg bhiorach dhìonach chothromach,
’S bu chorrach leam a sàil.

’N uair chaidh mi staigh do ’n Abailte,
Gum b’ ait an sealladh sùl
Bhith ’g amharc air na dealbhannan,				4955
Rìgh Fearghus ann air thùs;
A nis on rinn iad falbh uainn
Tha Alba gun an crùn;
’S e sin a dh’ fhàg na Garbhchriochan
’San aimsir seo a cùirt.					4960

Bidh lòchrain ann de ghloineachan,
Is coinneal anns gach àit,
A’ meudachadh an soilleireachd
Gu sealladh a thoirt dàibh;
Cha lugha ’n t-adhbhar éibhnis				4965
Cluig-chiùil ’gan éisdeachd ann,
’S gur binne na chuach Chéitein iad,
Le ’m forgan éibhinn ard.

Bidh faram air na coitseachan
’Nan trotan is ’nan deann,					4970
Eich nan cruaidh-cheum socrach,
Cha bhiodh an coiseachd mall;
Cùrsain mheamnach mhireanach,
A b’ àirde binneach ceann—
Chan e am fraoch a b’ innis daibh,				4975
No firichean nam beann.

Is ann an Clobhs’ a’ Pharlamaid
A chì mi thall an t-each,
’Na sheasamh mar a b’ àbhaist da
Air lom a’ chabhsair chlach;					4980

[TD 343]

[Beurla]

[TD 344]

Chuir iad srian is diallaid air,
’S e ’n rìgh a tha ’na glaic
’Gan robh còir na rìoghachd seo,
Ged dhìbir iad a mhac.

Tha taigh mór a’ Phàrlamaid					4985
Air àrdachadh le tlachd
Aig daoin’-uaisle ciallach
Nach tug riamh ach a’ bhreith cheart;
Tha breitheanas air thalamh ann
A mhaireas ’s nach téid as,					4990

’S thig na neochiontaich a mach.

A dhèanadh slàn gach dochartas				4995

Aon duine bhiodh an easlainte
No ’m freasdal ris an léigh,
B’ e sin an t-àite dleasdanach
Gu theasairginn o ’n eug.					5000

Tha Dùn Eideann bòidheach
Air iomadh seòl no dhà,
Gun bhaile anns an rìoghachd seo
Nach dèanadh strìocadh dhà;
A liuthad fear a dh’ ìnnsinn ann				5005

Daoin’-uaisle casg an ìota
Ag òl air fìon na Spàint’.

Ge mór a tha de dh’ astar

Na tha dh’ aitreabh ann air fad,
Nach ’eil ann as taitniche

Na taighean móra rìomhach					5015
Am bu chòir an rìgh bhith stad.

ORAN NAM BALGAIREAN

Ho hù o hó na balgairean,
O ’s ainmig iad r’ am faotainn!
Ho hù o hó na balgairean.

Mo bheannachd aig na balgairean,				5020
A chionn bhith sealg nan caorach.
Ho hù o hó na balgairean, &c.

An iad na caoraich cheannriabhach
Rinn aimhreit feadh an t-saoghail;

Am fearann a chur fàs oirnn,					5025
’S am màl a chur an daoiread?

Chan ’eil àit aig tuathanach,
Tha bhuannachd-san air claonadh;

Is éigin dhà bhith fàgail
An àit anns an robh dhaoine.					5030

Na bailtean is na h-àirighean
Am faighte blàths is faoileachd,

Gun taighean ach na làraichean,
Gun àiteach air na raointean.

Tha h-uile seòl a b’ àbhaist					5035
Anns a’ Ghàidhealtachd air caochladh,

Air cinntinn cho mì-nàdurra
’Sna h-àitean a bha aoigheil.

Chan ’eil loth no làir
Bhiodh searrach làimh r’ a taobh ann.			5040

[TD 347]

[Beurla]

[TD 348]

Chan ’eil aighean dàra
Bhios ag àrach an cuid laogh ann.

Chan ’eil feum air gruagaichean,
Tha h-uile buail’ air sgaoileadh.

Chan fhaigh gille tuarasdal					5045
Ach buachaille nan caorach.

Dh’ fhalbh na gobhair phrìseil;
Bu rìgh a dh’ òrdaich saor iad.

Earba bheag na dùslainn,
Cha dùisgear i le blaodhan.					5050

Chan ’eil fiadh air fuaran
On chaill na h-uaislean gaol daibh.

Gun duais a chionn a shaoithreach.

Is diombach air an duine mi					5055
A nì na sionnaich aoireadh;

A chuireas cù g’ an ruagadh
No thilgeas luaidhe chaol orr’.

Guma slàn na cuileanan
Tha fuireach ann an saobhaidh.				5060

Nam faigheadh iad mo dhùrachd,
Cha chùram dhaibh cion saoghail.

Bhiodh piseach air an òigridh,
Is bhiodh beò gus am marbh’ aois iad.

ORAN DO ’N INBHIR

Oidhche dhomh ’san Inbhir					5065
Bha lighe mhór an Conghlais
’S fhad’ a chual’ iad iomradh
Mu ’n iorghail ’san do thachair mi.
’S fhad’ a chual’ iad iomradh
Mu ’n iorghail ’san do thachair mi.				5070

Ghabh mi tàmh air thùs
Ann an seòrsa de thaigh ùdlaidh,
Is rinn mi suidhe sùmhail
Gus ’n do mhùth mi cairtealan.
Is rinn mi suidhe sùmhail, &c.				5075

Sin an t-am an d’ fhairich mi

Bha druim an taighe rùisgte,					5080

Bha grìosach bheag is móran smùid

Tàmh am bothan suarach,					5090
’S na cuarain mu na casan aic’?

[TD 352]

Ciod e rinn spòrsail uallach i,

’S ann fhuair e buain na cartach i.				5095

’S math an t-adhbhar-ghàire
Luchd-fanaid ’s fala-dhà i,
Chan ’eil i gabhail nàire
Ged chitheadh càch a’ marcachd i.

’S am fear tha laighe r’ a taobh,				5100

’S dùblaidh e na glasan air.

Ged tha iad làidir lìonmhor;
Am fad as beò ’san fhìonain e,				5110
Tha craobh chrìonaich aca-san.

A bhos is thall an Gallaibh iad,
’S e ’n call daibh nach do chailleadh
Am fear ud mun do bhaisteadh e.				5115

A mhilleas rùm gu fàs

Coimeasaidh luchd-eòlais					5120

’S e ’m pòr e nach dèan abachadh.

[TD 354]

Nighean Iain Bhuidhe ’s Calum ud,
’S i ’n uaisle ’n rud nach aithne dhaibh;			5125

A’ chuid as tàir’ de’n fhasan ud.

Gun mhios gun chliù gun fhortan,
An àros tàireil gortach,					5150
’S i bhochdainn a bha ’n tasgaidh ann.

Na bhuannaich iad air barganaibh,

Chan fharmadach am beartas e.				5155

[TD 356]

RAINN DO ’N CHEUD CHEAIRD

’S i cheud cheàird an tàillearachd,
O ’s ì rinn Adhamh air thùs,
A’ cheàird as luaith’ a ghnàthaicheadh,
’S gu bràth nach leig iad diùbh;				5175
Am fad ’s a bhios na màthraichean
A’ breith nam pàisdean rùisgt’,
Bidh feum air gnìomh na snàthaide
G’ an cumail blàth gu dlùth.

Chaidh Adhamh a chur ’sa’ Ghàrradh,			5180
Cha b’ e ’n t-àit ’n do chuir e dhùil;
Bu choma leis bhith saoithreachadh
Feadh chraobh a’ cur nam flùr;
Cha bheireadh e air sluasaid
’S cha ruamhradh e an ùir;					5185
Cha mhò a ghabh e coibe,
Chan oibricheadh e tùrn.

’S i Eubh’ a fhuaradh tàmailteach
Le dànadas gun tùr,
’N uair thug i ’n t-ubhal àlainn				5190
A bàrr a’ ghallain ùir;
’S truagh gun tug i dhà-san e,
Bu daor a phàigh e ’n sùgh—
Iad le chéile bhàsachadh,
’S na thàinig de shliochd dhiùbh.				5195

Chunnaic an sin Adhamh
Gun robh nochd ’s a nàire rùisgt’;
De ’n droigheann ghabh e snàthadan
’S rinn e snàth de ’n rùsg;
Dh’ fhuaigh e duilleagan nan geug				5200
Mu bheulaibh ’s air a chùl;
Dhiùlt e bhith ’na ghàrradair,
B’ e ’n tàillearachd a rùn.

[TD 359]

[Beurla]

[TD 360]

Ach fhaotainn le beachd sùl;
Gun snàth gun olainn chaorach,
Rinn e deise dh’ aodach ùr;
Bha e urramach ’na thàillear,					5210
Cha b’ fhear-gàrraidh e co-dhiùbh.

RAINN CLAIDHIMH

Gum bu slàn do làimh an Iarla
A chuir am charaibh
An claidheamh fhuair mi Di-ciadain
Ann am Bealach:						5215
Stàilinn chruadhach buadhmhor ciatach,
’S e geur tana,
Nach lùb ’s nach leumadh ’s nach beàrnadh
’S nach gabh camadh.

Claidheamh-cùil a choisinn cliù,				5220
Ged fhuair e fheuchainn;
’S tric a thug e buille drùiteach
Le làimh threubhaich;
Sàr cheann-Ileach làidir dìonach,
’S lann d’ a réir sin,						5225
Ghearradh e ubhal air uisge
Le fìor ghéiread.

Claidheamh lìthghorm nan trì chlaisean
Fhuair a chleachdadh ris na creuchdan,
B’ fheàirrde duin’-uasal ’na ghlaic e				5230
Nam biodh e ’san fheachd ag éirigh;
’S deas a laigheadh e air gaisgeach
’N uair rachadh e ceart ’na éideadh,
’S bhiodh ’ga ghiùlan an crios-gualainn
Air uachdar breacan an fhéilidh.				5235

’N uair a bha ’n saoghal an aimhreit
’S ann ’sa’ champ as tric a bhà e,
’S cha do chuir riamh fear a ghiùlain
Cùl r’ a nàmhaid;

[TD 363]

[Beurla]

[TD 364]

Gach duine tharraing a truaill e				5240
’S ann air a bha buaidh gach làrach;
’S e ’s fheàrr a thàinig riamh a ceàrdaich,
’S a rinneadh le Andra Faràra.

’S e rinn Andra ’n obair chiatach
A thoilicheadh miann gach Gàidheil;				5245
’S eireachdail e air an t-sliasaid,
’S cha mheasa gu gnìomh ’san làimh e;
Bha e tamall aig na Fiannaibh,
Daoine fiadhaich anns na blàraibh;
’S rinneadh e ’n toiseach do Dhiarmaid,			5250
’S ann aig sliochd Dhiarmaid a thà e.

ORAN DO IARLA BHRAGHAID ALBANN

Deoch-slàint’ an Iarla,
Cuir dian ’nar caraibh i,
’S ma gheibh sinn làn i
Gum fàg sinn falamh i;					5255
’N uair thig i òirnne
Gum bi sinn ceòlmhor,
’S gun gabh sinn òrain
’Ga h-òl gu faramach.

’S e ’n t-àrmann suairce					5260
A ghluais a Bealach leinn,
’S na sàr dhaoin’-uaisle
R’ a ghualainn mar ris ann;
On dh’ éirich sluagh leat
Gu feum ’sa’ chruadal,					5265
A réir do dhualchais
Bidh buaidh a dh’ aindeoin leat.

Gur deas am fiùran
Air thùs nan gallan thu,
’S cha ghabh thu cùram					5270
Roimh ghnùis nan aineolach;
Le d’ chòmhlainn ùra
’S tu féin ’gan stiùradh,
Is fir do dhùthcha
Ri d’ chùl mar bharantas.					5275

’S tu ceann na riaghailt
A tha ciallach carthannach;
Na daoin’ a thriall leat
Gur brèagh am pannal iad;
’S tu thog na ciadan						5280
A shliochd nam Fianntan,
’S an am a’ ghnìomha
Bu dian ’sa’ charraid iad.

[TD 367]

[Beurla]

[TD 368]

Ma thig na Frangaich
A nall do ’n fhearann seo,					5285
Bheir sinn tràth dhaibh
Cion-fàth an aithreachais;
Théid cuid gu bàs dhiubh,
’S cuid eile bhàthadh,
Mum faigh iad bàta						5290
’S mum fàg iad thairis sinn.

On fhuair sinn gunnachan,
Gur ullamh ealamh iad,
’S chan ’eil gin uile dhiubh
Nach freagair aingeal dhuinn;					5295
Chan fhaic na curaidhean
Dol sìos ’na chunnart dhaibh;
’S gur rìoghail urramach
A dhìoladh falachd iad.

’N uair théid gach treunfhear					5300
’Na éideadh ceannardach,
Le ’n armaibh gleusda
Cho geur ’s bu mhath leinn iad,

CEAD DEIREANNACH NAM BEANN

NOTES

In the following notes, metrical terms like ‘trochaic’ are introduced for simplicity; the term ‘rhyme’ indicates only correspondence of stressed vowel sounds; and names of syllabic metres are retained, though the verse does not conform to all the rules of old bardic versification.

Published versions of tunes have been noted for most of the songs commonly sung. In some instances the tune may vary from district to district, and the printed version is not, in many cases, identical with the traditional tune. This is clearly shown by the records made by Mr. J. L. Campbell in Uist and Barra of the songs numbered 6, 13, 14, 15, 18, 19, 21, 23, 30, 32, 62 in the Titles of Songs.

A tune for No. 41, recently broadcast, was supplied by Rev. J. K. Murchison, who noted it in Nova Scotia.

[Quotations are given without alteration.]


BATTLE OF FALKIRK
18th January, 1746

When Prince Charles learned that General Hawley was assembling a formidable force north-west of Falkirk, he drew off his army from the siege of Stirling to Plean Moor, and by swift manoeuvres gained the high ground on Falkirk Moor next day. Hawley was thus compelled to attack uphill, against a storm of rain as it happened; his cavalry could not operate freely over marshy country, and his artillery was bogged.

In their final positions the armies were separated by a sloping gully, narrow and deep at its upper end, wider and shallower at its lower end, where the Argyll Militia, a thousand strong, were placed in reserve. They were commanded by Colonel John Campbell of Mamore, afterwards fifth Duke of Argyll, and had joined Hawley’s army a few hours before the battle. The right wing of the Jacobite front consisted of MacGregors and Clan Donald regiments of Keppoch, Clanranald, and Glengarry; on the left, in the second line, was the French regiment.

Hawley, who had often declared that the clansmen would never stand up to a cavalry charge, ordered his dragoons to

[TD 422]

attack the Prince’s right wing; the Highlanders held their fire until the enemy was within easy range; their volley was so effective that the attack was broken, and the issue was really decided in these first few minutes. In their flight the dragoons rode over their own infantry, and the pursuing MacDonalds met no resistance from the disorganised militia. Apart from General Huske’s force, which was protected by the gully, the Hanoverian foot regiments failed to check the Highlanders’ advance, and the whole army retreated in disorder to Falkirk and thence towards Edinburgh, leaving stores and tents behind.

For a full account of the battle see The History of the Jacobite Rebellion, 1745–46, pp. 222–46, on which the foregoing note is based.

The two best-known Gaelic poets were directly involved in the stirring events of the “Forty-five.” Alexander MacDonald was a perfervid supporter of the Stuart cause, and a Captain in the Prince’s army, while Duncan Macintyre was a militiaman in the Hanoverian army, acting as a substitute for Archibald Fletcher of Crannach, who with other fencible men had been called up for military service by the Duke of Argyll, the Lord Lieutenant of the county. Service could be given either personally or by substitute, and Fletcher procured as his deputy the stalwart youth, Duncan Macintyre, promised him a fee of 300 merks and provided him with an ancient sword. The sword was lost in the Falkirk rout, and Fletcher refused to pay the promised fee when Duncan returned home, probably after the militia was disbanded in September 1746.

According to tradition, the debt was eventually paid through the intervention of Breadalbane, though it has to be noted that by this time the second Earl was so infirm that he left the management of his estates to his son. In any case, the poet obtained revenge by composing his first song and by hearing it sung throughout the district.

A footnote on page 1 of A, copied in later editions, reads:—’Se so ceud oran an ughdair (this is the author’s first song). It shows an ample vocabulary and characteristic touches of humour, though in his desire to justify the loss of the sword he overstresses its defects.

F follows A, with some changes in spelling.

The first stanza, as given in ABCDEF, is difficult to construe: line 4 ends with a semicolon, and line 7 begins ’S mur. This leaves line 5 an unrelated clause, and the interpretation of lines 7, 8 (had we not fled, we would not have fired, e.g. F, p. 3, Gram., p. 247) suggests that the militia rallied after their flight. This was not the case; line 8 is a simple statement of fact. In this text ’S of line 7 is omitted, and the punctuation is altered accordingly.

80. ABCDE, a bhuill; F, de bhuill; but de takes dat., and buill cannot be dat. sing. The gen. sing. with the article is common in such phrases, e.g. taghadh an eich, brod na sgine; cf. roghainn an t-sealgair, 927; taghadh na piocaid (AMD, p. 272).

To the appositive gen. idiom, e.g. amadan balaich, there is the alternative construction, amadan de bhalach; cf. tagha de dheagh chairt-iuil (MML 1221).

[TD 425]

SONG OF THE BREECHES

This spirited song was one of Macintyre’s earliest compositions. The opening lines would assign it to 1747, the year of the Disclothing Act. It was not included in the edition B (1790), presumably because the allusions to the reigning house, and the strong Jacobite sentiments of the poem, were considered in some quarters to be disloyal or offensive, although the Act had been repealed in 1782, and Macintyre’s own poem on the repeal was included in the edition.

In the Highlands this Act aroused bitter and enduring resentment, which found expression in songs by the leading Gaelic poets of the period. The Government’s trusted counsellor, Duncan Forbes of Culloden, declared that the Disclothing section of the Act was unwise and unnecessary.

The Act for pacifying the Highlands forbade (a) the possession or use of arms and (b) the wearing of the Highland garb or any part thereof. Penalties were severe: a second conviction made the wearer of a tartan garment liable to plantation servitude for seven years. Loyal supporters of the Government came under the same ban as the most rabid Jacobites; the people could not readily procure Lowland dress, even if they could afford it, and proud men were humiliated by having to appear in all sorts of makeshift garments, as the song indicates.

But the Government was determined to have no more Jacobite risings, and the official view of the Highland garb was probably well expressed in Burt’s Letters, when he wrote (Letter XXII, p. 171, Vol. II, 1815 ed.):

It is urged against it that it distinguishes the natives as a body of people distinct and separate from the rest of the subjects of Great Britain, and thereby is one cause of their narrow adherence among themselves to the exclusion of all the rest of the kingdom; but the part of the habit chiefly objected to is the plaid (or mantle), which, they say, is calculated for the encouragement of an idle life, in lying about on the heath in the daytime, instead of following some lawful employment; that it serves to cover them in the night when they lie in wait among the mountains to commit their robberies and depredations; and is composed of such colours as altogether, in the mass, so nearly resemble the heath on which they lie, that it is hardly to be distinguished from it, until one is so near them as to be within their power, if they have any evil intention; that it renders them ready at a moment’s notice

[TD 426]

to join in any rebellion, as they continually carry their tents about them; and lastly, it was thought necessary in Ireland to suppress that habit by act of parliament, for the above reasons, and no complaint for the want of it now remains among the mountaineers of that country.”

TITLE

A, Oran do’n Bhrigis; C, O. a Bhriogais; D, O. na Briogsa; E, O. nam Briogsan; F, O. do’n Briogais, but Contents page, Bhriogais. The plural form of “breeks” caused confusion.

TUNE

AC, Sean Triuthas Uilleam; DE, Uilleachan; F, Seann Triubhais Uilleam. The tune is noted in Songs of the Forty-five, p. 305, from S. Fraser Coll., No. 187.

METRE

The pattern of this U-poem is shown in the following table, where each letter represents a quatrain as printed:

RefrainStanza IStanza IIStanza IIIStanza IVStanza VStanza VILXLLLLLLXY3Y2,2Y2Y2Y3—ZY2ZY2ZZ—Y2Y2Y2Y2Y2Y2L may be written as two long lines, each having four stresses, internal rhyme and dactylic end-rhyme on u;

X has three phrases of two stresses, with trochaic end-rhyme, completed by a dactyl—in each half of the quatrain—
3 (’s olc an seòl duinn) duilichinn;

Y2 has three phrases of two stresses, with trochaic end-rhyme, repeated initially in the fourth line—
3 (na rinn e oirnn a dh’ anntlachd)
le ainneart a chumail ruinn;

Y3 like Y2, but with dactylic end-rhyme;

Z has four phrases of two stresses, with dactylic end-rhyme on u. The first stressed vowels also correspond throughout or in pairs.

[TD 427]

TEXT

110. rìgh: James “the Third,” the “Old Pretender.”

115. Rìgh Deòrsa: George II reigned from 1727 to 1760. He was the only son of George I, who was the grandson of Elizabeth, daughter of James VI. The House of Hanover could thus claim descent from the Stuarts, a fact which the poet overlooks. George II had two sons, Frederick and William. The former was the father of George III; the latter was the Duke of Cumberland, the notorious “Butcher.”

SONG TO THE MUSKET

This song was composed after the poet had left the Highlands and been enrolled in the Town Guard of Edinburgh. He had abandoned the stalker’s gun; but, while he appears to be well satisfied with his new life, his muse is not so happy in the urban environment. The most pleasing line in the song harks back to the stags in the forest.

The practice of giving personal names to weapons is an ancient one; but here the conceit by which the widow “Seònaid,” granddaughter of George, becomes the poet’s spouse and support, is over-elaborated. The song has some touches of humour and one revealing aphorism, but as a whole it is heavy.

‘Janet’ was a byname for a regimental firelock.

<gai>’S iad ’gam chur do dh’ arm Righ Deòrsa
’Ghiùlan “Seònaid” ’s còta dearg.<eng>
(Clàrsach na Coille, p. 1.)

METRE

This is an a-poem of the òran type. The stanza consists of four long lines, with four stresses and trochaic end-rhyme on a. The second stressed vowels may correspond in the four lines or in the couplets, or a line may have internal rhyme.

SONG TO A HALBERD

The Town Guard of Edinburgh was equipped with halberds; and this song, like the last, marks the poet’s enlistment in the force. It is a simple song, celebrating the poet’s satisfaction with his changed circumstances and the advantages derived from his espousal of Mary. It has the same personification as the previous song, and the figure leads to absurdity in certain lines.

The halberd was used by infantry from the fifteenth century. Its long shaft had a pointed metal end, below which was a double axehead; on one side the axehead was narrow and curved to a point.

Pennant (Tour, p. 190) refers to the “Lochaber axe, now used by none but the Town Guard of Edinburgh, a tremendous weapon.” The halberd was retained by sergeants of infantry to the end of the eighteenth century.

The Queen Mary of the title apparently refers to Mary II, who reigned jointly with William from 1689 to 1694.

General Hawley was commander-in-chief of the Hanoverian army at Falkirk, with little credit to himself. The poet had blamed him for lack of leadership in the battle.

James Colquhoun of Luss was a captain in the Black Watch in 1739; he served in Flanders and was invalided home, with the rank of Major, before 1745. In 1786 he was created a baronet (F, p. 483).

<gai>An Ridaire guineach,
Deagh Sheumas Cochunna.<eng>
(John MacGregor, Poems, p. 46.)

[TD 430]

TITLE

CDE, thailbheart; A, a fhuaireadh; BCD, a bha aig; E, a bh’ aig.

METRE

The stanza might be written as four long lines, each having four stresses and internal rhyme and end-rhyme on the last vowel. This is an òran metre.

TEXT

SONG TO THE KING

George III, born in 1738, reigned from 1760 to 1820. He was more acceptable to the British people than his predecessors of the Hanoverian line, and his long reign witnessed a great increase in British power and possessions, despite the loss of the American colonies. This poem is concerned with the earlier years of the reign.

Through the Hanoverian connection, Britain in alliance with Prussia became involved in the Seven Years War, which began when Russia, Austria and France attacked Prussia in 1756. The war started disastrously for Britain, but 1759 brought victories over France on sea and land, and in 1760 the whole of Canada was added to the Empire.

Charles III of Spain had resolved to gain Gibraltar and to exclude Britain from the South American markets. Pitt wished to declare war on Spain in 1761, but the young king declined. War was declared in 1762, and in the same year the Spanish possessions, Havana and Manila, were captured with much

[TD 431]

treasure. The invasion of Portugal by a Franco-Spanish army was checked by British troops landed at Lisbon in 1762.

In India Clive had defeated Surajah Dowlah, the Nabob of Bengal, in 1757; in 1764 Major Munro defeated the new Nabob at Buxar, and Bengal was ceded to the East India Company. In southern India French power was ended by Sir Eyre Coote’s victories at Wandewash in 1760 and Pondicherry in 1761. Thus Louis XV had suffered great losses before the Treaty of Paris brought hostilities to a close in 1763.

Some other historical references in the poem may be noted here.

(a) The Queen of Hungary was Maria Theresa, whose cause was supported by Britain against France and Prussia in the War of the Austrian Succession; but in the Seven Years War Austria was in alliance with France against Britain.

(b) The Seven Years’ War gave Pitt an opportunity of appealing to the Highlands for men to serve in the British armies. The swift and noble response to this gesture of confidence drew from him the eloquent tribute:

“I drew into your service a hardy and intrepid race of men. … These men were brought to combat on your side; they served with fidelity and they fought with valour, and conquered for you in every part of the world.”

(c) The revenues of the forfeited estates were earmarked by the Government for grants to encourage industry, agriculture and education in the Highlands, but only a small fraction of the total was in fact so used. (See Celtic Review, Vol. X.)

(d) General Wade constructed nearly 250 miles of military roads between 1725 and 1731. These ran from Inverness to Fort William, from Inverness to Dunkeld, from Fort Augustus to Dalwhinnie, from Crieff to Dalnacardoch, and from Catcleugh to Ruthven. His successors continued the programme of road-making, so that by 1767 nearly 1,000 miles of military roads were completed or in course of construction. Some of these roads would be familiar to Duncan Bàn, especially those radiating from Tyndrum to Dumbarton, to Inverary, to Fort William and to Callander. (See Wade in Scotland, p. 108.)

Many stretches of road were made by private enterprise and by “statute labour.” Pennant was surprised at the excellence of the roads from Loch Tay to Inverary by Tyndrum. The Earl of Breadalbane constructed the section from Kenmore to Glen Dochart at his own expense, but he received a grant of £1,000

[TD 432]

from the commissioners of the forfeited estates towards the cost of building the bridge over the Tay at Kenmore. (See Famed Breadalbane, p. 189.)

(e) The Act of 1696 laid on the heritors the duty of setting up a school in each parish, but where the population was scattered many districts could not benefit by this minimum requirement. The Church made some provision for remote communities, and the Society for the Propagation of Christian Knowledge sent teachers to open schools, usually for limited periods, in many Highland villages, with the aim of teaching old and young to read the Scriptures. The New Testament, translated into Gaelic by Rev. James Stuart of Killin, was published in 1767; and the first part of the Old Testament, translated by Rev. Dr Stuart of Luss, appeared in 1783. But a whole century passed after the publication of Macintyre’s poem before elementary education was brought within the reach of all.

METRE

Rannaigheachd bheag mhór. The couplet is of the form (8² + 8²), with aicill; the couplets rhyme.

LORD GLENORCHY

To explain certain references in this and other poems, some notes on the first three earls of Breadalbane may be conveniently given here.

John Campbell, younger of Glenorchy, born in 1635, was known in the Highlands as Iain Glas. As a youth of 22 years, this masterful man descended on London, and against all opposition

[TD 434]

married the beautiful and wealthy daughter of the Earl of Holland. In 1669 we find him in command of an expedition sent by the Privy Council to punish William Sinclair of Dunbeath for his forays into Sutherland. In addition to his own clansmen, Campbell had some Government troops and the assistance of George, sixth Earl of Caithness. He seems to have carried out his task to the satisfaction of the Council.

This Earl of Caithness was heavily in debt, and, having received large sums from Iain Glas from time to time, he ultimately conveyed to him, in settlement, not only his estates but his titles. Both were duly claimed on the death of the Earl in 1676, and next year Campbell actually became Earl of Caithness, Viscount of Breadalbane, Lord St Clair of Berridale and Glenorchy. But the rightful heir, George Sinclair of Keiss, had no difficulty in establishing his claim to the title, and the patent granted in error to Iain Glas was annulled. As compensation he received a new patent in 1681, whereby he was created Earl of Breadalbane and Holland, Viscount of Tay and Paintland, Lord Glenorchy, Benderaloch, Ormelie and Weick. An unusual provision was inserted at his request, giving him power to nominate any one of his sons as his successor.

To enforce his claim to the Caithness estates, Iain Glas marched north with 700 men and defeated the Sinclairs at Allt nam Mèirleach, having previously arranged that a quantity of whisky should be captured by the enemy. In the version of the story given by Pennant, a ship laden with whisky was deliberately stranded on the coast of Caithness (Tour, p. 183).

Only one other incident in the Caithness drama need be recorded here. Iain Glas married the widow of the Earl of Caithness in 1678, his first wife having died in 1666. Of this marriage there was one son, Colin, styled of Ardmadie, who died unmarried in 1708, reputed to be the father of John Campbell “of the Bank,” the subject of the next poem.

There were two sons of the first marriage, viz. Duncan, styled Lord Ormelie, born about 1660, and John, Lord Glenorchy, born in 1662. The former was excluded from the succession because he was alleged to be, on his own confession, simple-minded and easily imposed upon; but there was a persistent tradition in the Highlands that the real reason was the Earl’s fear that his estates would be confiscated if he were to designate Duncan, a strong Jacobite, as his successor. The latter with his two sons, Patrick and John, fought valiantly at Sheriffmuir and

[TD 435]

afterwards lived at Achinnischalain at the head of Glen Orchy. On the strength of this tradition Donald Campbell, Fort William, grandson of Patrick, unsuccessfully claimed the Breadalbane estates and titles in 1863.

It should be noted that Iain Glas evidently thought it desirable in 1681 that he should not be succeeded by his eldest son, and it would thus appear that his reasons were personal rather than political. Further, when the Earl was confined in Edinburgh Castle for alleged treason in 1695 it was not Lord Ormelie but Lord Glenorchy who journeyed to London and thence to Flanders to plead for his father. He saw King William at Namur, and soon afterwards the Earl was released. Lastly, it was Lord Glenorchy who was imprisoned in 1716 because of the part played by the Earl in the “Fifteen” rebellion, while the Earl himself was allowed, by reason of his age, to remain at Balloch.

The first Earl of Breadalbane died in 1717 and was duly succeeded by his second son. The second Earl was elected a Scottish representative peer in 1721, though not without protests by some of his fellow peers, who averred that he had no right to the Breadalbane title while his elder brother was still alive. He had a family of one son and two daughters. The son, John, Lord Glenorchy, born in 1695, succeeded his father in 1752.

This Lord Glenorchy had a noteworthy career. He entered Christ’s College, Oxford, in 1710 and had a distinguished record; he was a friend of Walpole, and in 1718 he was appointed Master of the Horse to the Princess Royal. In 1720 he was British Minister in Copenhagen and in 1731 Ambassador to the Russian Court; from 1727 to 1741 he was Member of Parliament for Saltash and a Lord of the Admiralty in 1741.

After the Battle of Prestonpans in 1745 Lord Glenorchy came north to Taymouth to take over the management of the estates, as his father was now too infirm to supervise his extensive territories. By his great influence and ability he succeeded in restricting the area of the rebellion.

Lord Glenorchy married in 1718 Amabel Gray, daughter of the Duke of Kent, with issue one son, who died at the age of 6 years, and one daughter. Lady Glenorchy died in 1727, and in 1730 Lord Glenorchy married Arabella, daughter of Sir John Pershall. There were two sons of this marriage, George and John; the former died in 1744, and the latter, born in 1738, was styled Lord Glenorchy. He married in 1761 and bought the property of Barnton, near Edinburgh, where he was well known as a young

[TD 436]

man about town. Contemporary references to him are not flattering. He died without issue in 1771, and the first Earl’s line failed. (See Famed Breadalbane, pp. 157–89; F, pp. 489–91.)

The subject of this poem is either the Lord Glenorchy who became the third Earl of Breadalbane or his son. Dr Calder (F, p. 486) says it was the latter, and attributes an error to the poet in the third stanza, where he describes the first Earl as Glenorchy’s grandfather. It is most improbable that Macintyre could have made such a mistake; nor can the poem, which describes a man of great charm and ability, who had played an important part in affairs and was already settled in Taymouth, be said to suit the younger man. In particular, lines 473–83 and 557–63 are quite inappropriate. It must, therefore, be concluded that the subject of this panegyric was the third Earl, and that the poem was written between 1746 and 1752, while he was still Lord Glenorchy, heir to the Breadalbane peerage and in residence at Taymouth. His record of achievement and public service made him a worthy subject of bardic praises.

TITLE

A, Ghlean-urchaidh; F, Ghleann Urchaidh; BCD, Mhor-fhear; mhor-fhir in 627. The O.G. form was mor-maer, where mor is the compositional form of muir. The o is shown to be short by the rhymes in 621–7. (See Bàrdachd vocab.)

METRE

The stanza consists of seven double-stressed phrases, having trochaic end-rhyme, completed by an amphibrach. The stress of the latter is on à throughout the poem. The seventh line in each stanza is repeated. The first stressed vowel in the phrases correspond throughout the stanza in more than half the poem. (7. (’s iomadh àit a bheil cliù ort) bhith càirdeach.)
